```json
{
  "fullTexts": [
    {
      "fetchError": null,
      "sourceFormat": "Formatted XML",
      "sourceUrl": "https://www.govinfo.gov/bulkdata/BILLS/119/2/hr/BILLS-119hr8365ih.xml",
      "text": "I\n119th CONGRESS\n2d Session\nH. R. 8365\nIN THE HOUSE OF REPRESENTATIVES\nApril 20, 2026 Mr. Biggs of Arizona (for himself, Mr. Fry , and Mr. Nehls ) introduced the following bill; which was referred to the Committee on the Judiciary\nA BILL\nTo provide for conditions on the appointment of monitors by courts, and for other purposes.\n#### 1. Short title\nThis Act may be cited as the Monitor Accountability Act of 2026 .\n#### 2. Conditions on the appointment of monitors by courts\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 90 days after the effective date of this section, the Administrator of the Administrative Office of the United States Courts shall by rule establish conditions on the appointment by a district court of the United States of any person charged, pursuant to a court order, with monitoring the conduct of a State or unit of local government. Such conditions shall include the following:\n**(1) Fees**\nSuch person\u2014\n**(A)**\nmay not assess a fee in excess of such maximum rates as the Administrator may establish; and\n**(B)**\nshall be authorized to employ the use of pro bono time or reduced rates.\n**(2) Exclusivity and term**\nSuch person may not be\u2014\n**(A)**\nappointed to more than one such monitorship at a time;\n**(B)**\nappointed for a term greater than 5 years; or\n**(C)**\nreappointed after the expiration of such term pursuant to the same court order.\n**(3) Subsequent monitors**\nA monitor who is appointed to a monitorship after the expiration of the term of a monitor who served pursuant to the same court order may not be employed by the same employer as the previous monitor.\n**(4) Public comment**\nPrior to the appointment of a monitor, the court shall provide notice of the person to be appointed and afford the public an opportunity for comment thereon.\n**(5) Termination**\n**(A) Revision**\nIn the case that a court, a party, or a monitor seeks to revise a monitorship imposed by a court order, the court shall conduct a hearing.\n**(B) Scope of monitorship**\nThe court may only revise a requirement of a monitorship with respect to which the subject of the monitorship has not attained substantial and sustained compliance.\n##### (b) Transfer\nOn the date that is 6 years after the court order imposing a monitorship, if such monitorship is in effect on such date, the case shall be transferred to another judge in the district in which the case is pending.\n##### (c) Accounting\n**(1) In general**\nOn an annual basis, a monitor shall submit to the court imposing the monitorship an accounting, which shall include\u2014\n**(A)**\ninformation on the services provided and the fee charged for such services; and\n**(B)**\nwhether any such services were provided pro bono or at a reduced rate.\n**(2) Publication**\nThe court shall make available to the public any accounting submitted to the court under paragraph (1).\n##### (d) Retroactivity\nIn the case of a monitorship that is in effect on the date of enactment of this Act and has been in effect for 6 years\u2014\n**(1)**\na new monitor shall be appointed not later than 180 days after such date of enactment in accordance with the limitations under this section; and\n**(2)**\nthe case shall be transferred not later than 1 year after such date of enactment in accordance with this section.\n##### (e) Sense of Congress\nIt is the sense of Congress that monitoring is a public service and monitorships should be structured to encourage the use of pro bono time or reduced rates.",
```

## API Data: summaries

```json
{
  "govinfoBulk": {
    "introducedDate": "2026-05-04",
    "originChamber": "House",
    "payload": {
      "dublinCore": {
        "contributor": "Congressional Research Service, Library of Congress",
        "description": "This file contains bill summaries for federal legislation. A bill summary describes the most significant provisions of a piece of legislation and details the effects the legislative text may have on current law and federal programs. Bill summaries are authored by the Congressional Research Service (CRS) of the Library of Congress. As stated in Public Law 91-510 (2 USC 166 (d)(6)), one of the duties of CRS is \"to prepare summaries and digests of bills and resolutions of a public general nature introduced in the Senate or House of Representatives\". For more information, refer to the User Guide that accompanies this file.",
        "format": "text/xml",
        "language": "EN",

          "summary-text": "<p><strong>Monitor Accountability Act</strong></p><p>This bill requires the Administrative Office of the U.S. Courts to establish conditions on the appointment of monitors to oversee state and local governmental entities. A <em>monitor</em> is an independent official appointed to oversee corrective reforms as part of a civil settlement agreement or consent decree, such as to remedy a pattern or practice of unconstitutional policing.</p><p>Among the conditions, this bill requires notice and an opportunity for public comment prior to the appointment of a monitor, limits an individual to one monitor appointment at a time, sets a five-year term limit for monitors, and requires a public accounting of the fees charged and services provided by the monitor. It also caps fees and explicitly authorizes the use of pro bono services.</p><p>In 2021, the Department of Justice began implementing a set of principles and specific recommendations regarding the use of monitors in civil settlement agreements and consent decrees involving state and local governmental entities, including recommendations relating to term limits, capping fees, and public accountability.\u00a0</p>"
```
